  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_d7a06415-9336-40fe-a64f-3507e61cd7df'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };
    if (typeof AppleID !== "undefined") {
      initAppleId();
    } else {
      initializeSiwa();
    }

<span id="freeTextContainer914278463645293784">We are the Dolophoni. Diligent. Vigilant. Fierce and inescapable.   <span id="freeText914278463645293784" style="display:none">We are the Dolophoni. Diligent. Vigilant. Fierce and inescapable. Servants of the Furies, we are the right hand of justice and no one stands before us.<br /><br />The son of Warcraft and Hate, Cratus spent eternity battling for the ancient gods who birthed him. He was death to any who crossed him. Until the day he laid down his arms and was banished into exile.<br /><br />Now an ancient enemy has been unleashed and our dreams are his chosen battlefield. The only hope we have is the one god who swears he will never fight again.<br /><br />As a Dream-Hunter, Delphine has spent eternity protecting mankind from the predators who prey on our unconscious state. But now that her allies have been turned, she knows in order to survive, the Dream-Hunters need a new leader. Someone who can train them to fight their new enemies. Cratus is her only hope. But she is a bitter reminder of why he chose to lay down his arms.<br /><br />Time is running out and if she can’t win him to her cause, mankind will be slaughtered and the world we know will soon cease to exist.</span>

          $$('div.prototip').each(function(i){i.setStyle({zIndex: $('box').getStyle('z-index')})});
        } else {
          $$('div.prototip').each(function(i){i.setStyle({zIndex: 6000})});
        }
      });
      $('rating_details_tip').observe('prototip:hidden', function () {
        $$('span.elementTwo').each(function (e) {
          if (e.getStyle('display') !== 'none') {
            var lessLink = e.next();
            swapContent(lessLink);
          }
        });
      });

//]]>
</script>  </div>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer1665602667" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7053722469751683653">4.25/5<br/><br/>I was pleasantly surprised by this awesome book. During the first 30% of the story, I thought it was an ok read for me, nothing particularly exciting and it didn’t fully capture me from the very start like other books by Kenyon did. But by the end, Dream Warrior totally went beyond my expectations! It was incredibly wonderful!<br/><br/>My eyes filled with tears as I read the beautiful and touching scene in the epilogue. I couldn’t be happier.<br/><br/>A very enjoyable read indeed!<br/></span>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2171586530" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11022876111328757484"><b>Cratus or Jericho (God of War) and Delphine Iole (demigod Oneroi)</b><br/><br/>Cratus is the guy who helped to imprison Prometheus. He has spent the majority of his life in Olympus as the lapdog of Zeus without thinking much. Until one day, he refused to murder an infant and his punishment was out of this world. Zeus took his godhood and Cratus was thrown to Earth where he had to live like a mortal. He could not accumulate money and wealth and he could not sleep in peace because every night his mortal heart w</span>
  <span id="freeText11022876111328757484" style="display:none"><b>Cratus or Jericho (God of War) and Delphine Iole (demigod Oneroi)</b><br /><br />Cratus is the guy who helped to imprison Prometheus. He has spent the majority of his life in Olympus as the lapdog of Zeus without thinking much. Until one day, he refused to murder an infant and his punishment was out of this world. Zeus took his godhood and Cratus was thrown to Earth where he had to live like a mortal. He could not accumulate money and wealth and he could not sleep in peace because every night his mortal heart was ripped out from his chest and the next morning a new heart was back in its place. <br /><br />Obviously Cratus hates Gods, obviously he wants revenge. So when Gods need his help, obviously he chooses to join the enemy, Noir and Azura (two out of the six first Gods who are pure concentrated evil). Now Crratus is called Jericho and he is out for blood.<br /><br />Delphine is sent by Zeus to try and convince Cratus to help them. During her attempts to approach him, she is captured by Noir and Azura and she is given to Cratus as a slave. She discovers that Scoti (the Oneroi slaves of emotions) help Noir and Azura, but only because the two evil Gods have been drugging Scoti during their dream state. <br /><br />Delphine and Cratus will fall in love and then Cratus will realize that not slaughtering this infant thousands of years ago, was one of the wisest decisions of his life.<br /><br />The mythology in this book is awesome. Old Greek myths and the author’s imagination are tangled together and produce an amazing complex world. It is one of the few times, we actually see Zeus in action and the whole Greek Gods and Goddesses pantheon takes sides and shows its cruelness and arrogance. Well done!<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="11022876111328757484" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1464605025" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1464605025" />
    <a title="Jilly" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/25894509-jilly"><img alt="Jilly" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1435955932p2/25894509.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1464605025?book_show_action=true">Dec 09, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jilly" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jilly" href="/user/show/25894509-jilly">Jilly</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25894509-jilly?shelf=urban-fantasy">urban-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25894509-jilly?shelf=paranormal-romance">paranormal-romance</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1464605025" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14317802744047094354">Based on the "love story" alone in this book, I was ready to polish up my 1-star rating for this one. But, luckily, a lot of other things happen that save it, and for that, I put my 1-star award away for another day.<br/><br/>I mean, I've seen a lot of insta-love in books, but this one... sheesh! <br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1449741121i/17332852.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/>If just saying a kind word to a gorgeous hunk of god-man is enough to make him fall instantly in love forever, I've got a lot of kind things to say to Chris Hemsworth!<br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1449741121i/17332853.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><i>well, hello gorgeous god-man...</i><br/><br/>Crap, spent to</span>
  <span id="freeText14317802744047094354" style="display:none">Based on the "love story" alone in this book, I was ready to polish up my 1-star rating for this one. But, luckily, a lot of other things happen that save it, and for that, I put my 1-star award away for another day.<br><br>I mean, I've seen a lot of insta-love in books, but this one... sheesh! <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1449741121i/17332852.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>If just saying a kind word to a gorgeous hunk of god-man is enough to make him fall instantly in love forever, I've got a lot of kind things to say to Chris Hemsworth!<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1449741121i/17332853.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><i>well, hello gorgeous god-man...</i><br><br>Crap, spent too much time looking at Hemsworth gifs. What was I talking about again? Oh, yeah, the crappy book. Okay, so it was crappy. The main guy, Jericho, had an eye-patch. I'm sorry, but I don't get the whole sexy eye patch thing. I mean, all I can think about is, "what is under that thing? Is it gross? Oh gosh, please don't let it come off and freak me out! Run away, run away!"<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1449741121i/17332854.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><i>Did you get a BB gun for Christmas?</i><br><br>The only saving part of this book was the fact that we got glimpses of the other Dark Hunters. Zarek, in particular, was sexily adorable. But, I have always had a weak spot for him. I love how him and his wife argue over the name of their son.<br><br><b>
  <i>"It's all right, Bob. Daddy's got you now. I'm saving you from Mommy's bad naming taste. I'd be crying too, if my mom named me after an idiot."<br><br>"Menoeceus is a great name," Astrid said defensively.<br><br>Zarek snorted. "For an old man or a feminine hygiene product. Not for my son. And next time I get to name the kid and it won't be something that sounds like meningitis."</i>
</b><br><br>There is enough Zarek sarcasm banter in this book for me to have given it an extra star, but be warned, not enough to tell anyone to read this book in the first place. I just found the tiny sliver of a ray of sunshine in an otherwise crap-fest.<br><br>So, should I explain why it's a crap-fest? I guess it's only fair. <br><br>First, the insta-love is ridiculous. <br><br>Second, the bad guys are completely new and not particularly interesting. Just simply, "me evil, me torture, me kill, end the world." Yeah, yeah, yeah... what else is new? Give us something we can use! And, what are the usual bad guys doing? Taking a break? <br><br>Third, there is a lot that happens, but it is almost too frantic. He's on earth, he's in some new realm that we've never heard of, he's in New Orleans eating, back to the new realm, over to earth again, now to Olympus, back, Stryker's realm, Hades realm, etc.. back and forth over an over again until I didn't know or care where the hell they were anymore. <br><br>And lastly, there was such predictability that I could have written the damn plot. He is thrown out of Olympus for sparing a baby's life, and that same baby grows up to be his one true love (within hours of meeting her). That's not a spoiler. You guess it immediately, then it is revealed early. It's truly the plot of bad Disney-ish children's stories.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1449741121i/17332855.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><i>disapproving father disapproves.</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="14317802744047094354" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer231833684" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer12150854999904717342">Sherrilyn Kenyon has, over the years and books, created the most original and ingenious series. <blockquote>
  
    <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1437592076i/15600627.jpg' alt=' photo 33655600e5c2113m3_zpsixbl2uf7.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
  
</blockquote>Choosing to walk into self-exile, after giving up fighting for the ancient Greek gods, Cratus/Jericho will be required to take up arms again if mankind and their world is to survive. But persuasion skills will have to be used if he’s to agree!<blockquote>
  
    <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1437592076i/15600628.jpg' alt=' photo jericho-145x145_zpskrem170f.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
  
</blockquote> Delphine, Dream-Hunter and mankind’s protector against the predators who invade their dreams is very dedicated and committed to her role</span>
  <span id="freeText12150854999904717342" style="display:none">Sherrilyn Kenyon has, over the years and books, created the most original and ingenious series. <blockquote>
  
    <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1437592076i/15600627.jpg" alt=" photo 33655600e5c2113m3_zpsixbl2uf7.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
  
</blockquote>Choosing to walk into self-exile, after giving up fighting for the ancient Greek gods, Cratus/Jericho will be required to take up arms again if mankind and their world is to survive. But persuasion skills will have to be used if he’s to agree!<blockquote>
  
    <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1437592076i/15600628.jpg" alt=" photo jericho-145x145_zpskrem170f.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
  
</blockquote> Delphine, Dream-Hunter and mankind’s protector against the predators who invade their dreams is very dedicated and committed to her role.<blockquote>
  
    <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1437592156i/15600642.jpg" alt=" photo delphine-145x145_zpsky3ppquk.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
  
</blockquote> When mankind is threatened with destruction, she will have to persuade Jericho to help her in overcoming the evil enemy.<br><br>I really liked Jericho and Delphine as a couple and their relationship and the banter between each other had some really great lines…….<blockquote>
  <b> “Why would you do that? (Delphine)<br>Why do you think? (Jericho)<br>Because I’m a bossy hag and you’d rather be enslaved to a man you hate than deal with me. (Delphine)<br>You know…you’re not funny. (Jericho)<br>I think I’m hysterical. (Delphine)” </b>
</blockquote> They were endearing and sweet and you wanted them to get their HEA.<br><br>There is so much happening in the story plot with so many characters that at times I had to remind myself whose story was this book about! I would have liked seeing more of them together.<br><br>The character development in the series just keeps getting better and better. <br><br>Oh, cliffhanger at the end…..just to wet your appetite…and wanting to get the next book!!</span>

<div id="review_3301080675" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3301080675" />
    <a title="Exina" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5309539-exina"><img alt="Exina" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1580809437p2/5309539.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3301080675?book_show_action=true">Apr 27, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Exina" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Exina" href="/user/show/5309539-exina">Exina</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/18857006-dream-warrior">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5309539-exina?shelf=pnr">pnr</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5309539-exina?shelf=confused-povs">confused-povs</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5309539-exina?shelf=great-characterization">great-characterization</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5309539-exina?shelf=greek-mythology">greek-mythology</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5309539-exina?shelf=abuse">abuse</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5309539-exina?shelf=multiple-pov">multiple-pov</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5309539-exina?shelf=great-secondary-characters">great-secondary-characters</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5309539-exina?shelf=action-and-thrill">action-and-thrill</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5309539-exina?shelf=alpha-males">alpha-males</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5309539-exina?shelf=badass-heroine">badass-heroine</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3301080675" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11130812121294270014"><b>Story</b><br/>6000 years earlier, Cratus, a sentinel of Zeus, had defied Zeus’ order and had spared a life he should have taken. He had been punished severely, his godhood taken, and forced to live on Earth as a mortal, deprived from even the tiniest morsel of happiness or satisfaction. Plus, he has been tortured and killed every night, and resurrected by the morning ever since.<br/><br/>The story sets in the present: the Greek pantheon is threatened by two Source gods, Noir and Azura. As Cratus (now Jericho) is a</span>
  <span id="freeText11130812121294270014" style="display:none"><b>Story</b><br />6000 years earlier, Cratus, a sentinel of Zeus, had defied Zeus’ order and had spared a life he should have taken. He had been punished severely, his godhood taken, and forced to live on Earth as a mortal, deprived from even the tiniest morsel of happiness or satisfaction. Plus, he has been tortured and killed every night, and resurrected by the morning ever since.<br /><br />The story sets in the present: the Greek pantheon is threatened by two Source gods, Noir and Azura. As Cratus (now Jericho) is a Source god himself, the Greeks send two Oneroi gods, Phobos and Delphine, to convince him to fight on their behalf, and in return he’d get back his godhood and powers. <br /><br />The first 30 percent is very repetitive and boring. The rest seems chaotic and soap-opera-like. New and old characters are thrown randomly into the plot: Greek Gods, Source Gods, Oneroi, Skoti, Atlanteans, Daimons, Dark-Hunters, Gallu demons, the “original gods of sun and of fire” – I’m not sure I mentioned everyone. Plus the maze in which they are all connected somehow. <br /><br /><b>Romance</b><br />The insta-love is justified with fate, no development.<br /><br /><b>Characters</b><br />Jericho is tortured yet he has compassion and a soft side – unexpected even for him. He is tall and handsome with a lethal aura, and insanely hot.<br /><br />Delphine is beautiful and perfect, with grace, a playful and caring attitude, and incredible fighting skills.<br /><br />By the way, in this world all of the male characters are insanely handsome and tall, with a lethal aura, and all the women are petite (except Astrid, who is tall), beautiful, funny and wise. <br /><br /><b>All in all</b><br />I read <i>Dream Warrior</i> two years ago, but I had to re-read it now because I didn’t review it then and I couldn’t remember a word from it. <br /><br />I started to read this series more than 10 years ago, and I loved it back then. But obviously, my reading taste has changed a lot, and I don’t enjoy PNR books as much as I did. I’ve abandoned not only this one, but many PNR series I had started to read because of the same reason. Sometimes I feel guilty about it, so I read the next one in line, but they usually don’t satisfy me. Sadly, it happened again with <i>Dream Warrior</i>.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11130812121294270014" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1770361723?book_show_action=true">Oct 02, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Gavin" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Gavin" href="/user/show/8192509-gavin">Gavin</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8192509-gavin?shelf=paranormal">paranormal</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1770361723" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17384435736461739708">This was another good entry in the Dark-Hunter series. Cratus(Jerich) and Delphine were both interesting characters and their romance was a fun one. Outside of the romance their was a ton of action.<br/><br/>Cratus was once Zeus's right hand. He was the man Zeus sent to enforce his justice. That all ended when he failed to obey one of the Greek God King's commands. Cratus was cursed to a life of eternal punishment. At least such would have been his fate if Zeus did not need him to deal with a problem that</span>
  <span id="freeText17384435736461739708" style="display:none">This was another good entry in the Dark-Hunter series. Cratus(Jerich) and Delphine were both interesting characters and their romance was a fun one. Outside of the romance their was a ton of action.<br /><br />Cratus was once Zeus's right hand. He was the man Zeus sent to enforce his justice. That all ended when he failed to obey one of the Greek God King's commands. Cratus was cursed to a life of eternal punishment. At least such would have been his fate if Zeus did not need him to deal with a problem that only he could solve. Dream Hunter Delphine is sent to tempt the surly hate filled ex-God back into the Olympus fold by any means necessary. <br /><br />The story was a fun one. There was plenty of humor and both Cratus and Delphine were easy characters to root for. Plenty happened in this instalment of the Dark-Hunters series as a new villain arrived on the scene and declared war on pretty much everyone. Those villains were the evil Noir and Azura. Both have potential and my only criticism is that we need to get to know them a bit better and learn what motivates them. Apollo, Apollymi, and Stryker have been such awesome villains, but I'm not complaining that the last two are on the road to redemption. It just means our new villains have big shoes to fill! <br /><br />This book had a ton of cameos. We got everyone from familiar Dream-Hunters to Olympian Gods and on to old favourites like Ash and Zarek. We also got more fun developments for characters such as Jayden, Jared, and Nick. Add to that the fact that we got to meet a crazy new demon and it meant fun times all around. <br /><br />This story felt like it was launching a new story arc in the Dark-Hunter series and even ended with a bit of a cliffhanger so I'm definitely looking forward to moving on to the next book in the series. <br /><br />Rating: 4 stars. <br /><br />Audio Note: William Dufris was not quite as good this time as he was when narrating the last book but he still did OK. <br /><br /><br /><br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="17384435736461739708" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer11086308149755374336">I think "Dream Warrior" is the first one of Sherrilyn Kenyon's Dream Hunter offshoot series that I really really liked. It wasn't the heroine who sucked me in this time, it was Cratus/Jericho all the way. His hardcore attitude for everyone but his gal just made me say, "Awww" and melt a little.<br/><br/>She's a Dream Hunter who determined to look for the best in others. He's the son of War and Hate who has been punished for centuries for showing mercy to a child. She's determined to get him to help the tr</span>
  <span id="freeText11086308149755374336" style="display:none">I think "Dream Warrior" is the first one of Sherrilyn Kenyon's Dream Hunter offshoot series that I really really liked. It wasn't the heroine who sucked me in this time, it was Cratus/Jericho all the way. His hardcore attitude for everyone but his gal just made me say, "Awww" and melt a little.<br /><br />She's a Dream Hunter who determined to look for the best in others. He's the son of War and Hate who has been punished for centuries for showing mercy to a child. She's determined to get him to help the trapped Olympians. As far as he's concerned, the only good Olympian is a dead one as none of them lifted a hand to help him. I'm guessing we might have some good conflict here!!<br /><br />I enjoyed watching Delphine and Jericho's relationship unfold. I found the pace and reasoning much more believable than others in this series. I loved the banter between Jericho and, well...just about everybody. That he was willing to give Delphine the time she needed (which, granted, wasn't much!) when he had been 'without' for so long caused another one of those "Awww" moments for me. And the icing on the cake was getting glimpses of the Dark Hunter crew once they lent their assistance to the cause.<br /><br />Hot and another keeper for me. Oh! The cover guy...Yum!</span>

<div id="review_1966812330" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1966812330" />
    <a title="Exina" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5309539-exina"><img alt="Exina" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1580809437p2/5309539.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1966812330?book_show_action=true">Apr 28, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Exina" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Exina" href="/user/show/5309539-exina">Exina</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/8120571-dream-warrior">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5309539-exina?shelf=gods-and-goddesses">gods-and-goddesses</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5309539-exina?shelf=greek-mythology">greek-mythology</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5309539-exina?shelf=pnr">pnr</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5309539-exina?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5309539-exina?shelf=great-secondary-characters">great-secondary-characters</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5309539-exina?shelf=favorite-authors">favorite-authors</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1966812330" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15998359882823011783"><b>Story</b><br/>6000 years earlier, Cratus, a sentinel of Zeus, had defied Zeus’ order and had spared a life he should have taken. He had been punished severely, his godhood taken, and forced to live on Earth as a mortal, deprived from even the tiniest morsel of happiness or satisfaction. Plus, he has been tortured and killed every night, and resurrected by the morning ever since.<br/><br/>The story sets in the present: the Greek pantheon is threatened by two Source gods, Noir and Azura. As Cratus (now Jericho) is a</span>
  <span id="freeText15998359882823011783" style="display:none"><b>Story</b><br />6000 years earlier, Cratus, a sentinel of Zeus, had defied Zeus’ order and had spared a life he should have taken. He had been punished severely, his godhood taken, and forced to live on Earth as a mortal, deprived from even the tiniest morsel of happiness or satisfaction. Plus, he has been tortured and killed every night, and resurrected by the morning ever since.<br /><br />The story sets in the present: the Greek pantheon is threatened by two Source gods, Noir and Azura. As Cratus (now Jericho) is a Source god himself, the Greeks send two Oneroi gods, Phobos and Delphine, to convince him to fight on their behalf, and in return he’d get back his godhood and powers. <br /><br />The first 30 percent is very repetitive and boring. The rest seems chaotic and soap-opera-like. New and old characters are thrown randomly into the plot: Greek Gods, Source Gods, Oneroi, Skoti, Atlanteans, Daimons, Dark-Hunters, Gallu demons, the “original gods of sun and of fire” – I’m not sure I mentioned everyone. Plus the maze in which they are all connected somehow. <br /><br /><b>Romance</b><br />The insta-love is justified with fate, no development.<br /><br /><b>Characters</b><br />Jericho is tortured yet he has compassion and a soft side – unexpected even for him. He is tall and handsome with a lethal aura, and insanely hot.<br /><br />Delphine is beautiful and perfect, with grace, a playful and caring attitude, and incredible fighting skills.<br /><br />By the way, in this world all of the male characters are insanely handsome and tall, with a lethal aura, and all the women are petite (except Astrid, who is tall), beautiful, funny and wise. <br /><br /><b>All in all</b><br />I read <i>Dream Warrior</i> two years ago, but I had to re-read it now because I didn’t review it then and I couldn’t remember a word from it. <br /><br />I started to read this series more than 10 years ago, and I loved it back then. But obviously, my reading taste has changed a lot, and I don’t enjoy PNR books as much as I did. I’ve abandoned not only this one, but many PNR series I had started to read because of the same reason. Sometimes I feel guilty about it, so I read the next one in line, but they usually don’t satisfy me. Sadly, it happened again with <i>Dream Warrior</i>.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15998359882823011783" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText10177058665646828983" style="display:none">Ok, so it was really hard to rate this book. A lot happens, so you must read it.<br /><br />While the love story here was a bit poor,the events that develop in this book are really interesting. Things between Jericho (Cratus) and Delphine happened too fast. They meet, they fall in love, the spend some days together, they get married.           <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">I have nooooo idea...</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2278800-anzu-the-great-destroyer?shelf=facepalm">facepalm</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer126200705" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16875487509088177222"><b>Review from <a href='http://zombiehazard.blogspot.com/2011/08/dream-warrior-dark-hunter-17.html' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'></a>ZombieHazard.</b><br/><br/><br/><b>My last ride on the Dark-Hunter bus</b><br/><br/>No, your eyes are not playing tricks on you. I can’t take Sherrilyn Kenyon’s endless and useless blabbering anymore. Dream Warrior is utter rubbish; you have the typical story that revolves around this series for OMG over 20 books. Seduce the dude or/and kill him. Kill the bad guys to save the world. Chick sees dude and falls for him even though they’re mortal enemies. Dude wants to kill chick but he can’t ‘cause she wakes up a flame in</span>
  <span id="freeText16875487509088177222" style="display:none"><b>Review from <a href="http://zombiehazard.blogspot.com/2011/08/dream-warrior-dark-hunter-17.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener"></a>ZombieHazard.</b><br><br><br><b>My last ride on the Dark-Hunter bus</b><br><br>No, your eyes are not playing tricks on you. I can’t take Sherrilyn Kenyon’s endless and useless blabbering anymore. Dream Warrior is utter rubbish; you have the typical story that revolves around this series for OMG over 20 books. Seduce the dude or/and kill him. Kill the bad guys to save the world. Chick sees dude and falls for him even though they’re mortal enemies. Dude wants to kill chick but he can’t ‘cause she wakes up a flame inside of him. Ugh why can’t they do something more original than this? At least if you plan to make this series endless put more effort in the damn stories.<br><br>I actually have a problem with Sherrilyn Kenyon. I consider this series long gone because even before <b>Acheron</b> most of the books weren’t so great anymore. I was in love with the series; there were many books I loved in the beginning of it. I fell in love with Ash the most and I couldn’t wait for his book. Bit by bit her books started to be unoriginal and repetitive. No characters that would catch your attention, mediocre and sucky stories and humor that didn’t bring any laughs out of me.<br><br>I’m actually thinking about what happened to the Dark-Huner series. Is Sherrilyn Kenyon out of ideas? Is she writing the books just for money or what? I guess there are still fans out there that love her books and probably still find them good. I don’t understand these people. Look I don’t wanna be mean or anything but doesn’t the lack of originality bother them? This series is not what it used to be. I would suggest the author to scratch it and start something new. But that’s probably just me…<br><br>You would wonder why I’m giving this speech right now. Well sadly I’m giving up the series so I thought it would be fair to explain why I’m doing it. There are many good PNRs out there who are actually worth reading. Dark-Hunter is not one of those anymore. I’ll try this author’s historicals and maybe <b> The Chronicles of Nick</b>.<br><br>One of the things that bothered me a lot was the humor in Dream Warrior. Sherrilyn Kenyon’s jokes are no funny anymore and they’re actually repetitive. What’s the fun of hearing the same phrase twice? And she is trying to make Jericho cool and tough and is failing miserably. He’s actually a perfect replica of the characters from book thirteen to book seventeen, excluding Ash of course.<br><br>What was good about the book? Probably seeing the characters I love. Ash (God I love this guy), Zarek (my second favorite character) and Jared (I’d like to read his story but I’m afraid it’ll be sucky so I’m confused). And that’s it with the good stuff. The rest of the book?<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380340457ra/696843.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I shouldn’t have to be happy to see these characters I love in order for me to like the books. I’d read characters’ books again and done. Happy day. This shouldn’t be the reason to continue reading the series. I’m actually feeling bad because I won’t get more of Ash, Jared, Savitar and Nick but I won’t curse my life by reading the rest of the books even for these dudes. Sorry guys!! Go beat up your maker and maybe things will get right!<br><br>It’s not cool that I ended up happy because I finished reading the book. I really wanted to love this but unfortunately I couldn’t. I’ll keep my eye out for the characters I like that might get books and maybe (<b>BIG MAYBE</b>) give them a try. Else I won’t bother.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16875487509088177222" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_94574039" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/94574039" />
    <a title="Sharon ∞❥ is an emotional book junkie ❥∞ " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3275325-sharon-is-an-emotional-book-junkie"><img alt="Sharon ∞❥ is an emotional book junkie ❥∞ " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1514769932p2/3275325.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/94574039?book_show_action=true">Mar 17, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sharon ∞❥ is an emotional book junkie ❥∞ " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sharon ∞❥ is an emotional book junkie ❥∞ " href="/user/show/3275325-sharon-is-an-emotional-book-junkie">Sharon ∞❥ is an emotional book junkie ❥∞ </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Mass Market Paperback 9780749909055" href="/book/show/2992069-dream-warrior">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3275325-sharon-is-an-emotional-book-junkie?shelf=read-in-2011">read-in-2011</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer94574039" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2896580495584629293">This is the book that ties all the Dream Hunters together. It also has Ash and a few other Dark Hunters in it, including Nick. (There's a nice little twist at the end with Madoc!)<br/><br/>Delphine and Jericho were really good together. I enjoyed how their story unfolded. Lots of little twists and surprises. <br/><br/>There were a bunch of other interesting characters, Jaden and Jared, to name a few. It was intriguing to see how intertwined everyone is. It also very frustrating and hard to keep straight all the nam</span>
  <span id="freeText2896580495584629293" style="display:none">This is the book that ties all the Dream Hunters together. It also has Ash and a few other Dark Hunters in it, including Nick. (There's a nice little twist at the end with Madoc!)<br /><br />Delphine and Jericho were really good together. I enjoyed how their story unfolded. Lots of little twists and surprises. <br /><br />There were a bunch of other interesting characters, Jaden and Jared, to name a few. It was intriguing to see how intertwined everyone is. It also very frustrating and hard to keep straight all the names and exactly what everyone is. It was also confusing because there are other series like this that use the same Gods and characters. I had to stop and remember who did what but I guess if you read enough PNR/UF, eventually you'll run into this. <br /><br />I would recommend reading the Dream Hunters. Obviously, it would have been better if I had read them in order with the Dark Hunters. You can check her website for the correct reading order:<br /><br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.sherrilynkenyon.com/book-series/dark-hunter/">http://www.sherrilynkenyon.com/book-s...</a><br /><br />If you decide to skip the Dream Hunters, you may miss out on some interesting tidbits!<br /><br />Favorite Line:<br /><br />"He took her hand into his and kissed her pale, unscarred knuckles. "We can be the blind leading the blind." <br /><br />Delphine squeezed his hand, "But as long as we're together..."<br /><br />"Nothing will ever touch us. You are all that matters to me, my angel, and I would walk through hell just to touch your face."</span>
  <a data-text-id="2896580495584629293" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_450518661" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/450518661" />
    <a title="AJ" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3143126-aj"><img alt="AJ" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1406382884p2/3143126.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/450518661?book_show_action=true">Nov 07, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="AJ" class="user" itemprop="url" name="AJ" href="/user/show/3143126-aj">AJ</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer450518661" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1530661232258546822"><b>
  <i>He was back.<br/>And he was pissed. May the Source take pity on those who’d caused his mood<br/>Because at the end of the day, he would have none for them. </i>
</b><br/><br/>Another Sherrilyn Kenyon book finished, and another hero that I have absolutely fallen in love with! Cratus is one of the MOST tortured heroes in the series. Banished from Olympus and cursed by Zeus himself (God, I hate that guy!), he has lived a miserable existence on earth for 6,000 years, continuously tormented by Zeus and his cronies. When it i</span>
  <span id="freeText1530661232258546822" style="display:none"><b>
  <i>He was back.<br />And he was pissed. May the Source take pity on those who’d caused his mood<br />Because at the end of the day, he would have none for them. </i>
</b><br /><br />Another Sherrilyn Kenyon book finished, and another hero that I have absolutely fallen in love with! Cratus is one of the MOST tortured heroes in the series. Banished from Olympus and cursed by Zeus himself (God, I hate that guy!), he has lived a miserable existence on earth for 6,000 years, continuously tormented by Zeus and his cronies. When it is realised that he has the power to defeat a new threat against the world, Olympus sends for him for help. But they are too late, with the bad guys getting to him first and recruiting him to their cause, promising to end his suffering. It is up to Dream Hunter, Delphine, to find Cratus (now going by the name Jericho), and bring him back to fight for the good guys – even if she has to seduce him to do it. <br /><br />Cratus/Jericho is an amazing character! An angry, violent warrior even before his exile, now he’s even more pissed off and antisocial. <br /><br /><i>(It) would have been tragic if Jericho were capable of feeling sympathy for someone else. He could appreciate it, but frankly, he didn’t care.</i><br /><br />But there’s something about Delphine that draws him to her, and he finds himself immediately protective of her. As a Dream Hunter who is half human, Delphine does have some emotion, and that is enough to spark a fiery attraction between them. <br /><br />I love the interactions between these two. He’s a big, scary warrior, and even though she’s small, she’s feisty and can more than handle herself. And before too long she starts to bring out a part of Jericho that he thought he had lost and there is some fantastic bantering. <br /><br /><i>“You really can’t help being an asshole, can you?”<br />“I probably could, but it’s not worth the effort.”</i><br /><br />With both of them having spent centuries alone, they are both desperate to feel some sort of affection, and it doesn’t take long for things to get steamy. And then when the romance comes… swooooooon! Who would have thought the big warrior would have it in him! <br /><br /><i>“You are all that matters to me, my angel, and I would walk through hell just to touch your face.”</i><br /><br />This book is an intense ride! It’s action packed from the very beginning, and doesn’t let up the whole way through. So much happens, with new bad guys Noir and Azura (evil, evil, evil) plotting to take over the world, starting with taking the Dream Hunters captive. It’s up to Jericho and Delphine – with a little help from series faves Acheron (squee), Zarek, Jaden and Jared (big plot developments here) to save the day. We also get introduced to the demon Asmodeus, who is freaking hilarious!<br /><br />There is a big action scene, but the climax of the book (which includes an epic smackdown!) is more of an introduction and preparation for a huge battle to come. And as usual, little hints are dropped and further twists and plotlines are set up for future books in the series that give you just enough information to drive you crazy with questions and wanting to know more!<br /><br />The series started with Dark Hunters vs Daimons, but it has become so much bigger than that! Kenyon has created an entire civilisation that mixes with mythology to become this massive world. It seems overwhelming at times, but the characters that she has given us that exist within her world all seem so real, and so easily blend with each other that it’s like you’re living the story right there with them. And I love that she consistently brings back characters from earlier books – there are a number of cameos in this story, and the epilogue had me squeeing like an idiot. But best cameo award goes to Zarek, with this little gem:<br /><br /><i>Astrid appeared with a crying toddler … Her face distressed, Astrid handed him off to Zarek. “Menoeceus wants his father.”<br />Zarek glared at her. “Bob is crying because he wants his mother to stop calling him that crap-ass name.” Zarek cuddled the small boy to him as he rocked him gently against his shoulder while he continued to wail. Loudly. “It’s all right, Bob. Daddy’s got you now. I’m saving you from Mommy’s bad naming taste. I’d be crying, too, if my mom named me after an idiot.”</i><br /><br />I loved it! 4.5 stars!<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="1530661232258546822" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_45278472" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/45278472" />
    <a title="The Flooze" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/355739-the-flooze"><img alt="The Flooze" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1599955192p2/355739.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/45278472?book_show_action=true">Feb 03, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="The Flooze" class="user" itemprop="url" name="The Flooze" href="/user/show/355739-the-flooze">The Flooze</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Mass Market Paperback 9780749909055" href="/book/show/2992069-dream-warrior">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/355739-the-flooze?shelf=owned">owned</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/355739-the-flooze?shelf=paranormal-romance">paranormal-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/355739-the-flooze?shelf=vanquished_2009">vanquished_2009</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer45278472" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10163081311775293622">I've loved the Dark Hunter series from the first book I read. I've been impressed with Kenyon's hold on her mythology and been intrigued with the mounting intricacies threading through the series as a whole. <br/><br/>But with this latest installment, and the full introduction of the new story arc, I find myself confused. In the last few novels, we've become increasingly aware of the Source and been introduced to a slew of new characters in relation to it. We've also learned some secrets about existing ch</span>
  <span id="freeText10163081311775293622" style="display:none">I've loved the Dark Hunter series from the first book I read. I've been impressed with Kenyon's hold on her mythology and been intrigued with the mounting intricacies threading through the series as a whole. <br /><br />But with this latest installment, and the full introduction of the new story arc, I find myself confused. In the last few novels, we've become increasingly aware of the Source and been introduced to a slew of new characters in relation to it. We've also learned some secrets about existing characters that will ensure their continued involvement in the series. <br /><br />While pleased that the author is willing to put a new spin on the series to keep it fresh, I can't help but feel a tad disappointed. <br /><br />Dream Warrior introduces this arc's big bad wolf, Noir. His appearance on the scene and rise to power is just thrown at us, only to be explained as an afterthought halfway through the novel. Compared to Kenyon's strong and thorough detailing of the Olympian pantheon, the introduction to this new and cruelly ambitious group seems ill-constructed. Noir and his cohorts do not have the suave appeal of Stryker. Nor do we understand Noir's motivation in his bid for power-unless you like the reason "just because." <br /><br />This new arc seems slapped together and disjointed. While I liked Jericho, the romantic relationship seemed forced, as did everything else until the action started midway through. <br /><br />Although Kenyon is trying to keep our interest by making these new foes mysterious, (only dribbling info on them here and there) she's not succeeding in fostering intrigue. And in the meantime, her attempt to keep us guessing prevents us from bonding with the characters (heroes and foes alike). I find myself so lacking in information about this new group that I don't really care about them. And it's not that it's a Dream Hunter novel-I loved Xypher's story and thought that the interaction between Arik and Solin was brilliant in the first Dream Hunter. <br /><br />For this new arc to work, I think Kenyon needs to tighten the concepts further and start offering more backstory. And she needs to hurry before we feel so distanced from the characters that we give up all together. <br /><br />Have to say though, I love Zarek and Bob. I love any appearance from Psycho-ass. And the new demon pal Asmodeus adds a fun touch. He reminds me of Kish from Sin's story. <br /><br />I'll carry on and read the next story, because, of course, I am completely addicted. But I do hope that by the next installment, Kenyon will have tightened the reins on the new elements and made the intricacies of her universe's mythology interesting and coherent again.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10163081311775293622" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2146266222" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

    <a title="Lauren" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4731410-lauren"><img alt="Lauren" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1387526203p2/4731410.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2146266222?book_show_action=true">Oct 07, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lauren" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lauren" href="/user/show/4731410-lauren">Lauren</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4731410-lauren?shelf=scarred-heroes">scarred-heroes</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4731410-lauren?shelf=tortured-hero">tortured-hero</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4731410-lauren?shelf=fated-mates">fated-mates</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4731410-lauren?shelf=new-orleans">new-orleans</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4731410-lauren?shelf=paranormal-romance">paranormal-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4731410-lauren?shelf=dreams">dreams</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2146266222" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8915080555046901874"><b>Dream Warrior</b><br/>3 Stars<br/><br/>The son of warcraft and hate, Cratus was one a trusted member of Zeus's personal guard. As a result of one fateful choice, Cratus was stripped of his power and cast out of Olympus to live as a mortal. Now, a malicious and powerful foe has targeted the Gods and Cratus aka Jericho is their only hope. Will he fight with those who spurned him or seek revenge by joining the ranks of their enemies?<br/><br/><u>Series note:</u> This is book # 4 in the Dream-Hunter series and book #17 in the Dark-Hun</span>
  <span id="freeText8915080555046901874" style="display:none"><b>Dream Warrior</b><br />3 Stars<br /><br />The son of warcraft and hate, Cratus was one a trusted member of Zeus's personal guard. As a result of one fateful choice, Cratus was stripped of his power and cast out of Olympus to live as a mortal. Now, a malicious and powerful foe has targeted the Gods and Cratus aka Jericho is their only hope. Will he fight with those who spurned him or seek revenge by joining the ranks of their enemies?<br /><br /><u>Series note:</u> This is book # 4 in the Dream-Hunter series and book #17 in the Dark-Hunter series. The is recommended that the books be read in order as there are numerous references to characters and events from previous installments. <br /><br />While this is one of the better stories in the series, it is still a far cry from the originality and excellence of the first few installments. The characters are one-dimensional, the romance is contrived and the sex scenes are stale. <br /><br />Jericho is identical to virtually every other Kenyon hero. He is tortured and abused, but finds the love of his life in Delphine, a Dream-Hunter, who just happens to be the <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[baby he sacrificed his life for in the first place <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> - very trite!<br /><br />Similarly, Delphine is a replica of the sweet yet shallow heroines from recent books and there is nothing really special or compelling about her personality. <br /><br />That said, there are some redeeming elements. The new story arc is developing in an intriguing direction although it is difficult to keep all of the characters and their affiliations straight. <br /><br />Moreover, some of the secondary characters have potential, especially Jared and Jaden despite the unfortunate and confusing similarity in their names. <br /><br />In sum, the series is losing momentum, but I have hopes that it will get back on track.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8915080555046901874" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_99948027" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/99948027" />
    <a title="Kelly" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/251943-kelly"><img alt="Kelly" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1385315310p2/251943.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/99948027?book_show_action=true">Apr 24, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kelly" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kelly" href="/user/show/251943-kelly">Kelly</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Mass Market Paperback 9780749909055" href="/book/show/2992069-dream-warrior">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/251943-kelly?shelf=physical-books">physical-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/251943-kelly?shelf=paranormal-romance">paranormal-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/251943-kelly?shelf=read-in-2013">read-in-2013</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/251943-kelly?shelf=read-in-2010">read-in-2010</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer99948027" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17704311671820511551">I think this is my favorite of the Dream-Hunter series. I don't know what it is about Jericho and Delphine that works for me, but I've reread this one a couple of times on the sly and it still drags me in and holds me captive until I'm done.<br/><br/>Wait. Maybe I do know. Let's take a look, shall we?<br/><br/>Jericho/Cratus has had a completely craptastic exile. Honestly, you'd think that the exile thing would be bad enough but the way Zeus punishes him is brutal. I'm not the hugest fan of Zeus as it is, but his a</span>
  <span id="freeText17704311671820511551" style="display:none">I think this is my favorite of the Dream-Hunter series. I don't know what it is about Jericho and Delphine that works for me, but I've reread this one a couple of times on the sly and it still drags me in and holds me captive until I'm done.<br /><br />Wait. Maybe I do know. Let's take a look, shall we?<br /><br />Jericho/Cratus has had a completely craptastic exile. Honestly, you'd think that the exile thing would be bad enough but the way Zeus punishes him is brutal. I'm not the hugest fan of Zeus as it is, but his actions toward Cratus and the reasoning behind why he cursed the Oneroi just cemented his douchcanoe status.<br /><br />Jerky gods are jerks.<br /><br />So, Jericho/Cratus has an awful life. He's wary of trusting anyone -- with good reason -- and he wants to wreak a little vengeance on the Greek pantheon. Frankly, I don't blame him. Delphine is the exact opposite of him. She trusts. She's unswervingly loyal. She doesn't back down when the people she loves are in danger.<br /><br />And this baffles Jericho. Man, watching as her kindness breaks through his walls makes me all mushy inside.<br /><br />Meanwhile, the bad guys are bad, the good guys have a little infighting going on, and we get some big movement in the overriding arc. The whole Jaden/Jared thing intrigues me. I want to see more of them and unravel what they are to one another and how they fit in overall.<br /><br />Onward.<br /><br />-Kelly @ <a href="http://paranormalbookreviews-kelly.blogspot.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Reading the Paranormal</a><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="17704311671820511551" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_148662318" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/148662318" />
    <a title="Diane " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4240167-diane"><img alt="Diane " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1360139658p2/4240167.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/148662318?book_show_action=true">Feb 16, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Diane " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Diane " href="/user/show/4240167-diane">Diane </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Mass Market Paperback 9780749909055" href="/book/show/2992069-dream-warrior">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer148662318" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14820987858563885435">"I pity those born of the lighter side. They have no understanding of how seductive cruelty is. "<br/>So far I'm team Noir and Azura. Hurray EVIL people!<br/><br/>------------------------------<br/><br/><br/>I did like Cratus and Delphine, but I wasn't very enthusiastic about them. Their love story wasn't really all that interesting to me. <br/><br/>As mentioned, Noir and Azura took the spotlight every time they're in a scene. Asmodeus did as well. He was both creepy and sweet, and I've grown fond of him.   <span id="freeText14820987858563885435" style="display:none">"I pity those born of the lighter side. They have no understanding of how seductive cruelty is. "<br />So far I'm team Noir and Azura. Because I need more of Nick and Pscho-ass in my life. :)<br /> <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />Not my favorite book in the bunch, but it has its moments. :)<br /></span>

<div id="review_505860205" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/505860205" />
    <a title="bibliophile ⭐️" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5829987-bibliophile"><img alt="bibliophile ⭐️" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1578045961p2/5829987.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/505860205?book_show_action=true">Jan 13, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="bibliophile ⭐️" class="user" itemprop="url" name="bibliophile ⭐️" href="/user/show/5829987-bibliophile">bibliophile ⭐️</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Mass Market Paperback 9780749909055" href="/book/show/2992069-dream-warrior">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5829987-bibliophile?shelf=adult-romance">adult-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5829987-bibliophile?shelf=lovable-hero">lovable-hero</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5829987-bibliophile?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5829987-bibliophile?shelf=betrayal">betrayal</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5829987-bibliophile?shelf=favorite-series">favorite-series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5829987-bibliophile?shelf=likable-characters">likable-characters</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5829987-bibliophile?shelf=re-read">re-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5829987-bibliophile?shelf=hurt">hurt</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5829987-bibliophile?shelf=cute-couple">cute-couple</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5829987-bibliophile?shelf=greek-mythology">greek-mythology</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer505860205" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9720787447605171592"><b>Dream Warrior</b> is another book from the <i>Dream Hunter series</i> - a spin off <b>Dark Hunter Series</b> by <i>Sherrilyn Kenyon</i> and I can say that I enjoyed it and I loved it. And will probably read it again and again and again like what I did with the previous books. <br/><br/>And it was the major turning point for the Dream-Hunters.<br/><br/><b>Dream Warrior</b> is the story of <i>
  <b>Cratus</b>
</i> or also known as <i>
  <b>Jericho</b>
</i> since Zeus stripped him of his godhood. He has been damned to live the rest of his life in pain and discomfort for betray</span>
  <span id="freeText9720787447605171592" style="display:none"><b>Dream Warrior</b> is another book from the <i>Dream Hunter series</i> - a spin off <b>Dark Hunter Series</b> by <i>Sherrilyn Kenyon</i> and I can say that I enjoyed it and I loved it. And will probably read it again and again and again like what I did with the previous books. <br /><br />And it was the major turning point for the Dream-Hunters.<br /><br /><b>Dream Warrior</b> is the story of <i>
  <b>Cratus</b>
</i> or also known as <i>
  <b>Jericho</b>
</i> since Zeus stripped him of his godhood. He has been damned to live the rest of his life in pain and discomfort for betraying an order from Zeus. And because of that he vowed to take revenge and decides to side with the enemy of the Greek Pantheon, Noir and his sister Azura, hoping that he'll get to kill Zeus in the process.<br /><br /><i>
  <b>Delphine</b>
</i> is an Oneroi Dream-Hunter and the one who was assigned by Zeus to find Cratus and convince him to help fight Noir and Azura because he is one of the few gods left that can derive power from the Source. <i>(And even after finishing the book, I still don’t know what/who the Source is. Argh!)</i> Then she was kidnapped by Azura and handed to Cratus as his slave.<br /><br />Because of what happened to him, Jericho was bitter and doesn’t trust easily but with Delphine he felt emotions that he swore he will never feel again. He became vulnerable and trusting. As for Delphine, he realized how horrid and painful his past as she got to know him and began to feel something towards him. I liked her even more because <i>she's the first person to show him tenderness and compassion... ever</i> Unbeknownst to them, they've already have connection even before they've met because Delphine is the baby whom Jericho saved. <br /><br />I absolutely enjoyed this one. One thing I've got to say about this world is that it's always growing. Each book opens some new aspect and introduces new characters. I got to know more about <b>Jaden</b> and <b>Jared</b> although I was getting them mixed up. And I think that there is so much more about them than we know, and I can’t wait to find out more about it. <br /><br />Then we have the chance to see <b>Tory</b> and <b>Ash</b> again, then there’s <b>Zarek</b> in all his bad-ass self again and <b>Astrid</b> also. <br /><br />Another thing that I loved about this one was <b>Nick</b> and <b>Ash</b> getting on again and back to their sarcastic selves. <i>Oh, I absolutely missed them!</i> And I’m hoping that by the time all is said and done <b>Nick and Ash will be best friends again.</b><br /><br /><i>Jericho choked in surprise. “This is the Malachai?”<br />Ash grinned wickedly. “In all his pain in the ass glory.”<br />Nick glowered at Ash. “Are we through now, Dad? Can I go play with my friends if I promise to be a good boy? I’ll even try and make it home by curfew.”</i><br /><br />Honestly, I can't wait for the next book in the series, and I hope that this series will never end. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="9720787447605171592" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Mass Market Paperback 9780749909055" href="/book/show/2992069-dream-warrior">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2478293-zeek?shelf=pnr">pnr</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2478293-zeek?shelf=pnr-kitchen-sink">pnr-kitchen-sink</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2478293-zeek?shelf=favorites-pnr">favorites-pnr</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2478293-zeek?shelf=vamps">vamps</a>,

          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer89352986" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1263328070929090044">Long ago, Cratus angered father god Zeus by not blindly obeying and got kicked out of Olympus. Still exiled on earth, the son of Warcraft and Hate is being called back to aid ol Thunderbutt himself. Only Cratus, now called Jericho, is not so interested in helping the fickle greek gods who turned their backs on him all those years ago.<br/><br/>When a pair of evil deities- who were formed from the source of all power- make him an offer that will return him to his god-like status, Cratus takes them up on it</span>
  <span id="freeText1263328070929090044" style="display:none">Long ago, Cratus angered father god Zeus by not blindly obeying and got kicked out of Olympus. Still exiled on earth, the son of Warcraft and Hate is being called back to aid ol Thunderbutt himself. Only Cratus, now called Jericho, is not so interested in helping the fickle greek gods who turned their backs on him all those years ago.<br /><br />When a pair of evil deities- who were formed from the source of all power- make him an offer that will return him to his god-like status, Cratus takes them up on it... but he's going to have to make war on Olympus to get what he wants.<br /><br />Delphine is an Oneroi- a member of the gods of Dreams who hunts the renegade Oneroi known as Skoti. Zeus has asked her to find Cratus and convince him to help fight the evil pair. In a twist of fate Delphine is kidnapped and given to Jericho as a slave. Naturally they fall for each other hook, line and sinker and a good thing too, because it will take both of them to untangle the sinister doings in this novel.<br /><br />A war is coming between Zeus and his children and those that have had it with their capricious ways. And it all starts here.<br /><br />Dream Warrior goes a long way in explaining why Zeus took such harsh measures against the Oneroi in the first place- forget what you've been told, there's an even more selfish reason and Delphine &amp; Jericho are at the heart of it.<br /><br />Many characters are at play in this novel as well as introduced, but if you have been following the Dark Hunters and Dream Hunters you won't have a problem keeping up.<br /><br />Oh and btw, more Dark Hunters are a-coming- you'll meet them in Dream Warrior as well.<br /><br />I truly enjoyed reading Dream Warrior. I found Jericho and Delphine's coming together to be some of the hottest kenyon's ever written. Sure there's a lot of the same themes going on in this one that Kenyon always puts in, but so what- that's why I come back to these novels.<br /><br />I find myself once again surprised by the fact that I am very interested in reading on in the series!</span>
  <a data-text-id="1263328070929090044" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <div class="left bodycol">

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Anyone who loves sarcastically dry humor, sexy characters, and kick ass fight scenes.</span></div>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Fangirl Musings by: </span>
      No one; but the series was recommended by a kind Books-A-Million
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1739253-fangirl-musings?shelf=classified-five-stars">classified-five-stars</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer45898473&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer45898473" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4103602973960794639">Holy GOD does this book kick some serious ass!!!<br/><br/>While that may be a seemingly over dramatic review notation, it most certainly applies to Dream Warrior. Not only is this action-packed from prologue to epilogue, the plot and characters being entertaining and fascinating as always, but there are some SERIOUS surprises within the novel!<br/><br/>1) Leta (Upon a Midnight Clear) is the mother of Delphine. <br/>2) Zeus never actually had the "Goat-Dream," but rather killed the half-blooded children of the Dream-Hunt</span>
  <span id="freeText4103602973960794639" style="display:none">Holy GOD does this book kick some serious ass!!!<br /><br />While that may be a seemingly over dramatic review notation, it most certainly applies to Dream Warrior. Not only is this action-packed from prologue to epilogue, the plot and characters being entertaining and fascinating as always, but there are some SERIOUS surprises within the novel!<br /><br />1) Leta (Upon a Midnight Clear) is the mother of Delphine. <br />2) Zeus never actually had the "Goat-Dream," but rather killed the half-blooded children of the Dream-Hunters in fear of a prophesy. <br />3) Jaden and Jared are definitely close, most probably brothers.<br />4) Jaden serves, and is tortured routinely by, Noir and Arazura (Source gods)<br />5) The Dream-Hunters get the emotions back as a result of Jericho being awesome.<br />6) Nick (The Malachai) is related to Madoc!<br />7) We meet the Dogs of War who, among being kick ass-able, are NOT regulated by the power drain or from hurting each other.<br /><br />Overall, this book is action packed, with a serious cliff hanger, and an unbelievable amount of entertainment! I started, and finished, the thing is less than 12 hours! Wrack another one up for the Mrs. AG!</span>
